    <!-- CentralNotice -->
   </div>
   <div class="mw-indicators">
   </div>
   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of songs recorded by Iron Maiden
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IronMaidencollage2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="736" data-file-width="649" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/IronMaidencollage2.jpg/220px-IronMaidencollage2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/IronMaidencollage2.jpg/330px-IronMaidencollage2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/IronMaidencollage2.jpg/440px-IronMaidencollage2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IronMaidencollage2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The current lineup of
        <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">
         Iron Maiden
        </a>
        comprises
        <a href="/wiki/Steve_Harris_(musician)" title="Steve Harris (musician)">
         Steve Harris
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Dave_Murray_(musician)" title="Dave Murray (musician)">
         Dave Murray
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Smith" title="Adrian Smith">
         Adrian Smith
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Dickinson" title="Bruce Dickinson">
         Bruce Dickinson
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Nicko_McBrain" title="Nicko McBrain">
         Nicko McBrain
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Janick_Gers" title="Janick Gers">
         Janick Gers
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">
       Iron Maiden
      </a>
      are an English
      <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">
       heavy metal
      </a>
      band formed by bassist
      <a href="/wiki/Steve_Harris_(musician)" title="Steve Harris (musician)">
       Steve Harris
      </a>
      in 1975. The band's first album, 1980's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden_(album)" title="Iron Maiden (album)">
        Iron Maiden
       </a>
      </i>
      was written primarily by Harris, with vocalist
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Di%27Anno" title="Paul Di'Anno">
       Paul Di'Anno
      </a>
      co-writing two tracks and guitarist
      <a href="/wiki/Dave_Murray_(musician)" title="Dave Murray (musician)">
       Dave Murray
      </a>
      contributing "Charlotte the Harlot".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ironmaiden_1-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ironmaiden-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The 1981 follow-up,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Killers_(Iron_Maiden_album)" title="Killers (Iron Maiden album)">
        Killers
       </a>
      </i>
      , was written almost entirely by the bassist, with frontman Di'Anno contributing only to the title track, "Killers" (North American bonus track "
      <a href="/wiki/Twilight_Zone_(Iron_Maiden_song)" title="Twilight Zone (Iron Maiden song)">
       Twilight Zone
      </a>
      " was credited to Harris and Murray).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-killers_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-killers-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Dickinson" title="Bruce Dickinson">
       Bruce Dickinson
      </a>
      replaced Di'Anno after the release of
      <i>
       Killers
      </i>
      , although did not contribute any songwriting to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Number_of_the_Beast_(album)" title="The Number of the Beast (album)">
        The Number of the Beast
       </a>
      </i>
      , released in 1982, which featured three songs co-written by guitarist
      <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Smith" title="Adrian Smith">
       Adrian Smith
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-numberofthebeast_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-numberofthebeast-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       The Number of the Beast
      </i>
      also spawned Iron Maiden's first
      <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">
       UK Singles Chart
      </a>
      top ten in the form of "
      <a href="/wiki/Run_to_the_Hills" title="Run to the Hills">
       Run to the Hills
      </a>
      ", which charted at number seven upon its release.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKcharts_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UKcharts-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was not until 1983's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Piece_of_Mind" title="Piece of Mind">
        Piece of Mind
       </a>
      </i>
      that the songwriting process became a more varied and collaborative approach, with just four of its nine tracks being credited solely to Harris, two to Dickinson and Smith, one to Harris and Murray, one to Dickinson alone, and one to Harris, Dickinson, and Smith.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pieceofmind_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pieceofmind-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Dickinson and Smith-penned "
      <a href="/wiki/Flight_of_Icarus" title="Flight of Icarus">
       Flight of Icarus
      </a>
      " was the first Iron Maiden single to chart in the United States, reaching number eight on the
      <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Rock_(chart)" title="Mainstream Rock (chart)">
       <i>
        Billboard
       </i>
       Mainstream Rock
      </a>
      chart.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UScharts_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UScharts-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Powerslave" title="Powerslave">
        Powerslave
       </a>
      </i>
      followed in 1984, which featured one of Iron Maiden's longest songs to date in the form of "Rime of the Ancient Mariner", written by Steve Harris and running almost 14 minutes in length.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-powerslave_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-powerslave-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Somewhere_in_Time_(Iron_Maiden_album)" title="Somewhere in Time (Iron Maiden album)">
        Somewhere in Time
       </a>
      </i>
      was notable for having both its singles written by someone other than Steve Harris, in this case Adrian Smith, who wrote three of the songs on the album.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-somewhereintime_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-somewhereintime-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Seventh_Son_of_a_Seventh_Son" title="Seventh Son of a Seventh Son">
        Seventh Son of a Seventh Son
       </a>
      </i>
      featured songwriting from a combination of Harris, Dickinson, Smith, and Murray,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seventhson_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-seventhson-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      before Smith left the group during the recording of its follow-up in 1990 having contributed to one song, "Hooks in You"; the resulting album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/No_Prayer_for_the_Dying" title="No Prayer for the Dying">
        No Prayer for the Dying
       </a>
      </i>
      , was the first to feature guitarist
      <a href="/wiki/Janick_Gers" title="Janick Gers">
       Janick Gers
      </a>
      , although he did not write any material for the record.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noprayer_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-noprayer-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was also the first to spawn a UK number-one single  Bruce Dickinson's "
      <a href="/wiki/Bring_Your_Daughter..._to_the_Slaughter" title="Bring Your Daughter... to the Slaughter">
       Bring Your Daughter... to the Slaughter
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKcharts_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-UKcharts-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gers contributed to his second album with Iron Maiden, 1992's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Fear_of_the_Dark_(Iron_Maiden_album)" title="Fear of the Dark (Iron Maiden album)">
        Fear of the Dark
       </a>
      </i>
      , co-writing three tracks with Dickinson, who would leave after the album's release, and two with Harris, who also produced for the first time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fearofthedark_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-fearofthedark-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1995, the band released
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(album)" title="The X Factor (album)">
        The X Factor
       </a>
      </i>
      , their first album since 1981's
      <i>
       Killers
      </i>
      without Bruce Dickinson on vocals.
      <a href="/wiki/Blaze_Bayley" title="Blaze Bayley">
       Blaze Bayley
      </a>
      replaced the frontman, and received songwriting credits for five of the album's eleven tracks, all of which were alongside Harris, Gers, or both.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thexfactor_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-thexfactor-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The band's first compilation album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Best_of_the_Beast" title="Best of the Beast">
        Best of the Beast
       </a>
      </i>
      , was released in 1993, which featured a new song and single in the form of "
      <a href="/wiki/Virus_(Iron_Maiden_song)" title="Virus (Iron Maiden song)">
       Virus
      </a>
      ", credited to Harris, Bayley, Murray, and Gers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bestofthebeast_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bestofthebeast-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Bayley recorded a second album with Iron Maiden,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Virtual_XI" title="Virtual XI">
        Virtual XI
       </a>
      </i>
      , on which he only contributed songwriting for three songs, the rest being written almost entirely by Harris.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-virtualxi_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-virtualxi-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Both Dickinson and Smith returned to the band for the recording of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Brave_New_World_(Iron_Maiden_album)" title="Brave New World (Iron Maiden album)">
        Brave New World
       </a>
      </i>
      , the first Iron Maiden album produced by
      <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Shirley" title="Kevin Shirley">
       Kevin Shirley
      </a>
      (alongside Harris), which was released in 2000 and spawned two UK top-20 singles in the form of "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Wicker_Man_(song)" title="The Wicker Man (song)">
       The Wicker Man
      </a>
      " and "
      <a href="/wiki/Out_of_the_Silent_Planet_(song)" title="Out of the Silent Planet (song)">
       Out of the Silent Planet
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKcharts_4-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-UKcharts-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another largely collaborative album, only one song ("Blood Brothers") was written by Harris alone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bravenewworld_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bravenewworld-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The 2003 follow-up,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Dance_of_Death_(album)" title="Dance of Death (album)">
        Dance of Death
       </a>
      </i>
      , was even more commercially successful than
      <i>
       Brave New World
      </i>
      , and also featured the first track in the band's history to be written with long-term drummer
      <a href="/wiki/Nicko_McBrain" title="Nicko McBrain">
       Nicko McBrain
      </a>
      , "New Frontier".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danceofdeath_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-danceofdeath-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Matter_of_Life_and_Death_(album)" title="A Matter of Life and Death (album)">
        A Matter of Life and Death
       </a>
      </i>
      , the band's first release to chart in the top ten of the US
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">
       <i>
        Billboard
       </i>
       200
      </a>
      albums chart,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UScharts_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-UScharts-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      was released in 2006 and was largely written by Harris, Dickinson, and Smith, with Gers and Murray also contributing to a couple of tracks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifeanddeath_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lifeanddeath-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Final_Frontier" title="The Final Frontier">
        The Final Frontier
       </a>
      </i>
      , released in 2010, was their first album since
      <i>
       Fear of the Dark
      </i>
      to top the
      <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">
       UK Albums Chart
      </a>
      and was another collaborative effort from the band, with Harris, Dickinson, and Smith again leading the songwriting.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefinalfrontier_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-thefinalfrontier-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       The Final Frontier
      </i>
      also led to the band's first
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
       Grammy Award
      </a>
      win, as single "
      <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_(Iron_Maiden_song)" title="El Dorado (Iron Maiden song)">
       El Dorado
      </a>
      " won the award for
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance">
       Best Metal Performance
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/53rd_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="53rd Annual Grammy Awards">
       2011 ceremony
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Their upcoming 2015 studio album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Souls" title="The Book of Souls">
        The Book of Souls
       </a>
      </i>
      , is their longest to date, at 93 minutes, and their first double album.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOS_ann_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BOS_ann-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also features "Empire of the Clouds", written by Dickinson, which surpasses "Rime of the Ancient Mariner" as the band's longest song.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Since their formation, Iron Maiden have also released numerous additional songs as
      <a href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side" title="A-side and B-side">
       B-sides
      </a>
      to their singles, including original songs and
      <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">
       cover versions
      </a>
      . A collection of these B-sides were compiled and released in the form of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Best_of_the_%27B%27_Sides" title="Best of the 'B' Sides">
        Best of the 'B' Sides
       </a>
      </i>
      , one of three albums included in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Eddie%27s_Archive" title="Eddie's Archive">
        Eddie's Archive
       </a>
      </i>
      box set released in 2002.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eddiesarchive_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-eddiesarchive-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Included on this album was a range of B-sides released since the band's formation, including originals "Burning Ambition" (Harris), "Black Bart Blues" (Harris, Dickinson), and "Justice of the Peace" (Harris, Murray), and covers "
      <a href="/wiki/Cross-Eyed_Mary" title="Cross-Eyed Mary">
       Cross-Eyed Mary
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/Jethro_Tull_(band)" title="Jethro Tull (band)">
       Jethro Tull
      </a>
      ), "
      <a href="/wiki/Communication_Breakdown" title="Communication Breakdown">
       Communication Breakdown
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">
       Led Zeppelin
      </a>
      ), and "
      <a href="/wiki/My_Generation" title="My Generation">
       My Generation
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">
       The Who
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bestofthebsides_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bestofthebsides-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album also contained 1988 re-recordings of
      <i>
       Iron Maiden
      </i>
      tracks "Prowler" and "Charlotte the Harlot", released as B-sides to "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Evil_That_Men_Do_(song)" title="The Evil That Men Do (song)">
       The Evil That Men Do
      </a>
      ",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theevilthatmendo_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-theevilthatmendo-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a 1999 live version of "
      <a href="/wiki/Wasted_Years" title="Wasted Years">
       Wasted Years
      </a>
      " from the 1986 album
      <i>
       Somewhere in Time
      </i>
      , released as a B-side to "Out of the Silent Planet" in 2000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silentplanet_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-silentplanet-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Iron Maiden also contributed a cover of
      <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">
       Deep Purple
      </a>
      's "
      <a href="/wiki/Space_Truckin%27" title="Space Truckin'">
       Space Truckin'
      </a>
      " to the 2012 tribute album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Re-Machined:_A_Tribute_to_Deep_Purple%27s_Machine_Head" title="Re-Machined: A Tribute to Deep Purple's Machine Head">
        Re-Machined: A Tribute to Deep Purple's Machine Head
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-remachined_26-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-remachined-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Songs">
       Songs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_songs_recorded_by_Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Songs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steve_Harris_30nov2006.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="921" data-file-width="827" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Steve_Harris_30nov2006.jpg/220px-Steve_Harris_30nov2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Steve_Harris_30nov2006.jpg/330px-Steve_Harris_30nov2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Steve_Harris_30nov2006.jpg/440px-Steve_Harris_30nov2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steve_Harris_30nov2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Since their inception, the majority of the band's songwriting has been led by founding member
        <a href="/wiki/Steve_Harris_(musician)" title="Steve Harris (musician)">
         Steve Harris
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IRON_MAIDEN_-_Manchester_Apollo_-_1980.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4760" data-file-width="3522" height="297" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/IRON_MAIDEN_-_Manchester_Apollo_-_1980.jpg/220px-IRON_MAIDEN_-_Manchester_Apollo_-_1980.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/IRON_MAIDEN_-_Manchester_Apollo_-_1980.jpg/330px-IRON_MAIDEN_-_Manchester_Apollo_-_1980.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/IRON_MAIDEN_-_Manchester_Apollo_-_1980.jpg/440px-IRON_MAIDEN_-_Manchester_Apollo_-_1980.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IRON_MAIDEN_-_Manchester_Apollo_-_1980.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Harris and original vocalist
        <a href="/wiki/Paul_Di%27Anno" title="Paul Di'Anno">
         Paul Di'Anno
        </a>
        wrote three tracks together for the band's first two albums: "Remember Tomorrow", "
        <a href="/wiki/Running_Free" title="Running Free">
         Running Free
        </a>
        ", and "Killers".
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Dickinson_2008.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="683" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bruce_Dickinson_2008.jpg/220px-Bruce_Dickinson_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bruce_Dickinson_2008.jpg/330px-Bruce_Dickinson_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bruce_Dickinson_2008.jpg/440px-Bruce_Dickinson_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Dickinson_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Since joining the band in 1981, vocalist
        <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Dickinson" title="Bruce Dickinson">
         Bruce Dickinson
        </a>
        has contributed consistently to Iron Maiden's songwriting, including their first number-one single, "
        <a href="/wiki/Bring_Your_Daughter..._to_the_Slaughter" title="Bring Your Daughter... to the Slaughter">
         Bring Your Daughter... to the Slaughter
        </a>
        ".
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adrian_Smith_Iron_Maiden_Newcastle.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1608" data-file-width="1410" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Adrian_Smith_Iron_Maiden_Newcastle.jpg/220px-Adrian_Smith_Iron_Maiden_Newcastle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Adrian_Smith_Iron_Maiden_Newcastle.jpg/330px-Adrian_Smith_Iron_Maiden_Newcastle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Adrian_Smith_Iron_Maiden_Newcastle.jpg/440px-Adrian_Smith_Iron_Maiden_Newcastle.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adrian_Smith_Iron_Maiden_Newcastle.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Guitarist
        <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Smith" title="Adrian Smith">
         Adrian Smith
        </a>
        has also written numerous songs for the band since joining in 1980, often working with Dickinson and/or Harris on compositions.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Davemurray.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="683" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Davemurray.jpg/220px-Davemurray.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Davemurray.jpg/330px-Davemurray.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Davemurray.jpg/440px-Davemurray.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Davemurray.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        As the second longest-serving member of the band,
        <a href="/wiki/Dave_Murray_(musician)" title="Dave Murray (musician)">
         Dave Murray
        </a>
        has contributed songwriting to almost every Iron Maiden album since their inception.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iron_Maiden_Janick_Gers.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="2592" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Iron_Maiden_Janick_Gers.jpg/220px-Iron_Maiden_Janick_Gers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Iron_Maiden_Janick_Gers.jpg/330px-Iron_Maiden_Janick_Gers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Iron_Maiden_Janick_Gers.jpg/440px-Iron_Maiden_Janick_Gers.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iron_Maiden_Janick_Gers.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Janick_Gers" title="Janick Gers">
         Janick Gers
        </a>
        joined Iron Maiden in 1990, and has since co-written a number of songs for the band, mainly alongside Harris.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iron_Maiden_en_Costa_RicaNicko.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="683" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Iron_Maiden_en_Costa_RicaNicko.jpg/220px-Iron_Maiden_en_Costa_RicaNicko.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Iron_Maiden_en_Costa_RicaNicko.jpg/330px-Iron_Maiden_en_Costa_RicaNicko.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Iron_Maiden_en_Costa_RicaNicko.jpg/440px-Iron_Maiden_en_Costa_RicaNicko.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iron_Maiden_en_Costa_RicaNicko.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Despite being a member of the band since 1982, it took until 2003 for drummer
        <a href="/wiki/Nicko_McBrain" title="Nicko McBrain">
         Nicko McBrain
        </a>
        to write a song for Iron Maiden, namely "New Frontier" for
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Dance_of_Death_(album)" title="Dance of Death (album)">
          Dance of Death
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:070918--blaze_bayley.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1185" data-file-width="1200" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/070918--blaze_bayley.jpg/220px-070918--blaze_bayley.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/070918--blaze_bayley.jpg/330px-070918--blaze_bayley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/070918--blaze_bayley.jpg/440px-070918--blaze_bayley.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:070918--blaze_bayley.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        During his brief tenure with the band, vocalist
        <a href="/wiki/Blaze_Bayley" title="Blaze Bayley">
         Blaze Bayley
        </a>
        helped write eight songs on the two Iron Maiden albums on which he performed,
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(album)" title="The X Factor (album)">
          The X Factor
         </a>
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Virtual_XI" title="Virtual XI">
          Virtual XI
         </a>
        </i>
        , as well as "
        <a href="/wiki/Virus_(Iron_Maiden_song)" title="Virus (Iron Maiden song)">
         Virus
        </a>
        ".
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
